### Description of the condition

Depression is the leading cause of ill health and disability in the world, affecting over 280 million people \[[1](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0001 "World Health Organisation. Depressive disorder (depression). https://www.who.int/news-room/fact-sheets/detail/depression (accessed 1 November 2023)."), [2](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0002 "GBD 2019 Mental Disorders Collaborators. Global, regional, and national burden of 12 mental disorders in 204 countries and territories, 1990-2019: a systematic analysis for the Global Burden of Disease Study 2019. Lancet. Psychiatry2022;9(2):137-50. [DOI: 10.1016/S2215-0366(21)00395-3]")\]. Its effects are felt throughout all regions, irrespective of whether they consist of high‐income or low‐income and middle‐income countries \[[3](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0003 "World Health Organization. Depression and other common mental disorders. Global health estimates. https://www.who.int/mental_health/management/depression/prevalence_global_health_estimates/en/2017.")\]. The prevalence of depression has continued to rise, increasing by more than 18% between 2005 and 2015, reflecting both population growth and an ageing population \[[3](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0003 "World Health Organization. Depression and other common mental disorders. Global health estimates. https://www.who.int/mental_health/management/depression/prevalence_global_health_estimates/en/2017.")\]. Although some studies suggest that the incidence of depression is becoming more stable globally \[[4](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0004 "ZhangY , JiaX , YangY , SunN , ShiS , WangW . Change in the global burden of depression from 1990-2019 and its prediction for 2030. Journal of Psychiatric Research2024;178:16-22. [DOI: 10.1016/j.jpsychires.2024.07.054]")\], specific events such as the COVID‐19 pandemic and 'lockdown' dramatically affected its prevalence \[[5](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0005 "World Health Organisation. COVID-19 pandemic triggers 25% increase in prevalence of anxiety and depression worldwide. https://www.who.int/news/item/02-03-2022-covid-19-pandemic-triggers-25-increase-in-prevalence-of-anxiety-and-depression-worldwide2022.")\]. Depression has a considerable effect on peoples’ health, their functioning, disease outcomes, hospital‐seeking behaviour and length of life \[[4](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0004 "ZhangY , JiaX , YangY , SunN , ShiS , WangW . Change in the global burden of depression from 1990-2019 and its prediction for 2030. Journal of Psychiatric Research2024;178:16-22. [DOI: 10.1016/j.jpsychires.2024.07.054]"), [6](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0006 "MoussaviS , ChatterjiS , VerdesE , TandonA , PatelV , UstunB . Depression, chronic diseases, and decrements in health: results from the World Health Surveys. Lancet2007;370(9590):808-9."), [7](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0007 "SeymourJ , BenningTB . Depression, cardiac mortality and all-cause mortality. Advances in Psychiatric Treatment2009;15(2):107-13.")\]. Depression was the second main cause of non‐fatal ill‐health or disability globally in 2021, accounting for approximately 47 million years lived with disability (YLD) (6.1% of all YLD) \[[8](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0008 "Agudelo-BoteroM , Giraldo-RodríguezL , Rojas-RussellM , González-RobledoMC , Balderas-MirandaJT , Castillo-RangelD , et al. Prevalence, incidence and years of life adjusted for disability due to depressive disorders in Mexico: results of the Global Burden of Disease Study 2019. Journal of Affective Disorders Reports2021;6:-. [DOI: 10.1016/j.jadr.2021.100206]")\]. In 2021, mortality associated with suicide accounted for 727,000 deaths worldwide \[[9](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0009 "World Health Organisation. Suicide worldwide in 2021. Global health estimates. https://www.who.int/publications/i/item/97892401100692021.")\]. Although it is a global concern, the effects of depression have been felt disproportionately in low‐ and middle‐income countries, where over 80% of the world's non‐fatal disease burden and 78% of suicides were reported in 2015 \[[3](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0003 "World Health Organization. Depression and other common mental disorders. Global health estimates. https://www.who.int/mental_health/management/depression/prevalence_global_health_estimates/en/2017.")\].

Depression encompasses a broad and varied range of mental health concerns. It is typified by persistent low mood; sadness; loss of pleasure in most activities and experiences; and is associated with emotional, cognitive, physical and behavioural symptoms \[[10](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0010 "National Institute for Health and Clinical Excellence. Depression in adults: recognition and management. http://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/CG902009.")\]. People with depression may experience a loss of energy, a change in appetite, altered sleep patterns, anxiety, reduced concentration, indecisiveness, restlessness, feelings of worthlessness, guilt or hopelessness, and thoughts of self‐harm or suicide \[[3](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0003 "World Health Organization. Depression and other common mental disorders. Global health estimates. https://www.who.int/mental_health/management/depression/prevalence_global_health_estimates/en/2017.")\]. It can be a long‐lasting or recurring condition, affecting a person’s ability to function and cope with daily life. The diagnosis and the severity of depression are determined by the extent of the symptoms incurred and the level of functional impairment. The fifth edition of the Manual of Mental Disorders (DSM‐V) classifies major depressive disorders as the occurrence of at least five out of nine symptoms and a decline in a person’s daily functioning \[[11](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0011 "American Psychiatric Association. Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders, Fifth Edition. Arlington: Arlington, 2013. [DOI: 10.1176/appi.books.9780890425596]")\]. The effects and severity of these symptoms have to be felt throughout each day and persist for at least two weeks \[[10](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0010 "National Institute for Health and Clinical Excellence. Depression in adults: recognition and management. http://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/CG902009."), [11](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0011 "American Psychiatric Association. Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders, Fifth Edition. Arlington: Arlington, 2013. [DOI: 10.1176/appi.books.9780890425596]")\]. Importantly, at least one of the symptoms experienced has to be depressed mood or loss of interest or pleasure \[[11](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0011 "American Psychiatric Association. Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders, Fifth Edition. Arlington: Arlington, 2013. [DOI: 10.1176/appi.books.9780890425596]")\]. The DSM‐V classifies severity of depression into three categories: mild (a few symptoms more than is required for diagnosis but these do not have a significant impact), moderate (number and intensity of symptoms between mild and severe) and severe (number of symptoms are substantially above what is required for diagnosis and subsequent symptoms are unmanageable and distressing, and interfere with social and occupational functioning) \[[11](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0011 "American Psychiatric Association. Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders, Fifth Edition. Arlington: Arlington, 2013. [DOI: 10.1176/appi.books.9780890425596]")\].

### Description of the intervention and how it might work

Depression is treatable. It is treated with antidepressants, psychological therapies, alternative approaches or a combination of these options. Antidepressants are effective for the treatment of depression in primary care, especially for people with more than minor depression \[[12](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0012 "ArrollB , ElleyCR , FishmanT , Goodyear-SmithFA , KenealyT , BlashkiG , et al. Antidepressants versus placebo for depression in primary care. Cochrane Database of Systematic Reviews2009, Issue 3. Art. No: CD007954. [DOI: 10.1002/14651858.CD007954]"), [13](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0013 "LindeK , KristonL , RuckerG , JamilS , SchumannI , MeissnerK , et al. Efficacy and acceptability of pharmacological treatments for depressive disorders in primary care: systematic review and network meta-analysis. Annals of Family Medicine2015;13(1):69–79.")\]. In addition to benefiting the acutely ill, antidepressants can help reduce the risk of relapse into depression \[[10](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0010 "National Institute for Health and Clinical Excellence. Depression in adults: recognition and management. http://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/CG902009."), [14](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0014 "GeddesJR , CarneySM , DaviesC , FurukawaTA , KupferDJ , FrankE , et al. Relapse prevention with antidepressant drug treatment in depressive disorders: a systematic review. Lancet2003;361(9358):653–61."), [15](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0015 "NICE. Depression in adults: treatment and management. https://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/ng2222022.")\]. Recommendations for their use are often as part of combined treatment with high‐intensity psychological interventions (cognitive behavioural therapy (CBT) or interpersonal therapy (IPT)) \[[10](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0010 "National Institute for Health and Clinical Excellence. Depression in adults: recognition and management. http://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/CG902009."), [15](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0015 "NICE. Depression in adults: treatment and management. https://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/ng2222022.")\]. The effectiveness of antidepressants in managing depression may be tempered by several concerns, including: adverse side effects that impact on people’s health and quality of life \[[16](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0016 "FergusonJM . SSRI antidepressant medications: adverse effects and tolerability. Primary Care Companion to the Journal of Clinical Psychiatry2001;3(1):22-7."), [17](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0017 "KellyK , PosternakM , AlpertJE . Toward achieving optimal response: understanding and managing antidepressant side effects. Dialogues in Clinical Neuroscience2008;10(4):409-18."), [18](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0018 "AndrewsPW , ThomsonJA , AmstadterA , NealeMC . Primum non Nocere: an evolutionary analysis of whether antidepressants do more harm than good. Frontiers in Psychology2012;24(3):1-19."), [19](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0019 "OlivaV , LippiM , PaciR , Del FabroL , DelvecchioG , BrambillaP , et al. Gastrointestinal side effects associated with antidepressant treatments in patients with major depressive disorder: a systematic review and meta-analysis. Progress in Neuro-Psychopharmacology & Biological Psychiatry2021;109(110266):-. [DOI: 10.1016/j.pnpbp.2021.110266]")\]; a lag time between starting antidepressants and improvements in mood \[[20](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0020 "Machado-VieiraR , SalvadoreG , LuckenbaughDA , ManjiHK , ZarateCA . Rapid onset of antidepressant action: a new paradigm in the research and treatment of major depressive disorder. Clinical Psychiatry2008;69(6):946-58.")\]; and poor adherence \[[21](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0021 "TamburrinoMB , NagelRW , ChahalMK , LynchDJ . Antidepressant medication adherence: a study of primary care patients. Primary Care Companion to the Journal of Clinical Psychiatry2009;11(5):205-11."), [22](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0022 "SansoneRA , SansoneLA . Antidepressant adherence: are patients taking their medications?Innovations in Clinical Neuroscience2012;9(5):41-6.")\].

Psychological treatments provide another option, particularly if antidepressants are not effective or are poorly tolerated \[[10](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0010 "National Institute for Health and Clinical Excellence. Depression in adults: recognition and management. http://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/CG902009."), [15](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0015 "NICE. Depression in adults: treatment and management. https://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/ng2222022.")\]. Their use may be as an adjunct to other interventions, particularly antidepressants, or as a standalone intervention \[[10](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0010 "National Institute for Health and Clinical Excellence. Depression in adults: recognition and management. http://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/CG902009."), [15](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0015 "NICE. Depression in adults: treatment and management. https://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/ng2222022.")\]. Increasingly, the use of psychological therapies is being recommended in different countries \[[10](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0010 "National Institute for Health and Clinical Excellence. Depression in adults: recognition and management. http://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/CG902009."), [15](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0015 "NICE. Depression in adults: treatment and management. https://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/ng2222022."), [23](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0023 "Scottish Intercollegiate Guidelines Network. Non-pharmaceutical management of depression in adults. http://www.sign.ac.uk/pdf/sign114.pdf2010."), [24](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0024 "American Psychological Association. APA clinical practice guideline for the treatment of depression across three age cohorts. Available at https://www.apa.org/depression-guideline/guideline.pdf2019."), [25](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0025 "American College of Physicians 2016. Nonpharmacologic versus pharmacologic treatment of adult patients with major depressive disorder: a clinical practice guideline from the American College of Physicians. Annals of Internal Medicine2016;164(5):350-9."), [26](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0026 "ParikhSV , QuiltyLC , RavitzP , RosenbluthM , PavlovaB , GrigoriadisS , et al; Uher R; CANMAT Depression Work Group. CANMAT depression work group. Canadian network for mood and anxiety treatments (CANMAT) 2016 clinical guidelines for the management of adults with major depressive disorder: section 2. Psychological treatments. Canadian Journal of Psychiatry2016;61(9):524-39."), [27](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0027 "Royal Australian and New Zealand College of Psychiatrists. Australian and New Zealand clinical practice guidelines for the treatment of depression. Australian and New Zealand Journal of Psychiatry2004;38(6):389-407."), [28](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0028 "WolfNJ , HopkoDR . Psychosocial and pharmacological interventions for depressed adults in primary care: a critical review. Clinical Psychology Review2008;28(1):131-61."), [29](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0029 "ParikhSV , SegalZV , GrigoriadisS , RavindranAV , KennedySH , LamRW , et al. Canadian Network for Mood and Anxiety Treatments (CANMAT) clinical guidelines for the management of major depressive disorder in adults. II. Psychotherapy alone or in combination with antidepressant medication. Journal of Affective Disorders2009;117(1):S15-S25.")\], reflecting their effectiveness irrespective of the severity of depression, the population being treated or the care setting \[[30](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0030 "CuijpersP , AnderssonG , DonkerT , Van StratenA . Psychological treatment of depression: results of a series of meta-analyses. Nordic Journal of Psychiatry2011;65(6):354-64."), [31](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0031 "OrgetaV , QaziA , SpectorA , OrrellM . Psychological treatments for depression and anxiety in dementia and mild cognitive impairment: systematic review and meta-analysis. British Journal of Psychiatry2015;207(4):293-8.")\]. Despite the apparent benefits of psychological treatments, their effectiveness depends on people’s expectations, perceived stigma, sustained motivation, degree of psychological mindedness and the influence of possible side effects (e.g. emotional discomfort, increased stress, resurfacing of memories, or physical problems (e.g. sleep problems, tiredness, headaches))\[[32](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0032 "CooneyGM , DwanK , GreigCA , LawlorDA , RimerJ , WaughFR , et al. Exercise for depression. Cochrane Database of Systematic Reviews2013, Issue 9. Art. No: CD004366. [DOI: 10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub6]"), [33](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0033 "BarlowDH . Negative effects from psychological treatments: a perspective. American Psychologist2010;65(1):13-20."), [34](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0034 "BrittTW . Perceived stigma and barriers to care for psychological treatment: implications for reactions to stressors in different contexts. Journal of Social and Clinical Psychology2008;27(4):317-35. [DOI: 10.1521/jscp.2008.27.4.317]")\].

Other approaches have also been used as alternatives to, or to supplement, pharmacological and psychological treatments. These include music therapy, light therapy, acupuncture, family therapy, marital therapy, exercise, relaxation therapy and other complementary techniques \[[35](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0035 "SolomonD , AdamsJ . The use of complementary and alternative medicine in adults with depressive disorders. A critical integrative review. Journal of Affective Disorders2015;179:101-13."), [36](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0036 "MeekumsB , KarkouV , NelsonEA . Dance movement therapy for depression. Cochrane Database of Systematic Reviews2015, Issue 2. Art. No: CD009895. [DOI: 10.1002/14651858.CD009895.pub2]"), [37](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0037 "JoyceJ , HerbisonGP . Reiki for depression and anxiety. Cochrane Database of Systematic Reviews2015, Issue 4. Art. No: CD006833. [DOI: 10.1002/14651858.CD006833.pub2]"), [38](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0038 "AalbersS , Fusar-PoliL , FreemanRE , SpreenM , KetJC , VinkAC , et al. Music therapy for depression. Cochrane Database of Systematic Reviews2017, Issue 11. Art. No: CD004517. [DOI: 10.1002/14651858.CD004517.pub3]"), [39](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0039 "TaoL , JiangR , ZhangK , QianZ , ChenP , LvY , et al. Light therapy in non-seasonal depression: an update meta-analysis. Psychiatry Research2020;291(113247):-. [DOI: 10.1016/j.psychres.2020.113247]")\]. The increasing use of alternative interventions for treating depression may reflect dissatisfaction with conventional treatments, people’s beliefs and philosophies influencing their treatment choice, and the possibility that alternative treatments may be effective \[[35](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0035 "SolomonD , AdamsJ . The use of complementary and alternative medicine in adults with depressive disorders. A critical integrative review. Journal of Affective Disorders2015;179:101-13."), [40](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0040 "AstinJA . Why patients use alternative medicine: results of a study. JAMA1998;279(19):1548-53.")\].

Exercise has received growing attention as an approach to managing depression, whether as part of stepped‐care programmes, combination therapy or monotherapy \[[15](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0015 "NICE. Depression in adults: treatment and management. https://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/ng2222022."), [32](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0032 "CooneyGM , DwanK , GreigCA , LawlorDA , RimerJ , WaughFR , et al. Exercise for depression. Cochrane Database of Systematic Reviews2013, Issue 9. Art. No: CD004366. [DOI: 10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub6]"), [41](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0041 "BlumenthalJA , SmithPJ , HoffmanBM . Is exercise a viable treatment for depression?ACSM's Health & Fitness Journal2012;16(4):14-21."), [42](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0042 "CraftLL , PernaFM . The benefits of exercise for the clinically depressed. Primary Care Companion to the Journal of Clinical Psychiatry2004;6(3):104-11."), [43](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0043 "EkkekakisP . Honey, I shrunk the pooled SMD! Guide to critical appraisal of systematic reviews and meta-analyses using the Cochrane review on exercise for depression as example. Mental Health and Physical Activity2015;8:21-36."), [44](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0044 "MalhiGS , BellE , BassettD , BoyceP , BryantR , HazellP , et al. The 2020 Royal Australian and NewZealand College of Psychiatrists clinical practice guidelines for mood disorders. Australian and New Zealand Journal of Psychiatry2021;55(1):7-117. [DOI: 10.1177/0004867420979353]"), [45](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0045 "StubbsB , VancampfortD , HallgrenM , FirthJ , VeroneseN , SolmiM , et al. EPA guidance on physical activity as a treatment for severe mental illness: a meta-review of the evidence and Position Statement from the European Psychiatric Association (EPA), supported by the International Organization of Physical Therapists in Mental Health (IOPTMH). European Psychiatry2018;54:124-44. [DOI: 10.1016/j.eurpsy.2018.07.004]")\]. It is defined as the “planned, structured and repetitive bodily movement done to improve or maintain one or more components of physical fitness” \[[46](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0046 "American College of Sports Medicine. ACSM's Resource Manual for Guidelines for Exercise Testing and Prescription. 4th edition. Lippincott, Williams and Wilkins, 2001.")\]. The effect of exercise on depression has been the subject of research for several decades, with evidence continuing to emerge that assesses its effectiveness for different severities of depression (e.g. mild, moderate or severe), population groups (e.g. age, sex), management approaches (e.g. preventative, first‐line or second‐line) and against different comparators (e.g. usual care, waiting list, antidepressants, psychological treatments) \[[47](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0047 "BeesleyS , MutrieN . Exercise is beneficial adjunctive treatment in depression. BMJ (Clinical Research Ed.)1997;315(7121):1542-3."), [48](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0048 "AndelV , GlenE , AustinD . Physical fitness and mental health: a review of the literature. Adapted Physical Activity Quarterly1984;3(1):207."), [49](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0049 "SilveiraH , MoraesH , OliveiraN , CoutinhoES , LaksJ , DeslandesA . Physical exercise and clinically depressed patients: a systematic review and meta-analysis. Neuropsychobiology2013;67(2):61-8."), [50](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0050 "De Souza MouraAM , LamegoMK , PaesF , Ferreira RochaNB , Simoes-SilvaV , RochaSA , et al. Comparison among aerobic exercise and other types of interventions to treat depression: a systematic review. CNS & Neurological Disorders - Drug Targets2015;14(9):1171-83."), [51](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0051 "SchuchFB , VancampfortD , RichardsJ , RosenbaumS , WardPB , StubbsB . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis adjusting for publication bias. Journal of Psychiatric Research2016;77:42-51."), [52](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0052 "FarahWH , AlsawasM , MainouM , AlahdabF , FarahMH , AhmedAT , et al. Non-pharmacological treatment of depression: a systematic review and evidence map. Evidence-based Medicine2016;21(6):214-21."), [53](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0053 "DanielssonL , NorasAM , WaernM , CarlssonJ . Exercise in the treatment of major depression: a systematic review grading the quality of evidence. Physiotherapy Theory and Practice2013;29(8):573-85."), [54](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0054 "StubbsB , VancampfortD , RosenbaumS , WardPB , RichardsJ , UssherM , et al. Challenges establishing the efficacy of exercise as an antidepressant treatment: a systematic review and meta-analysis of control group responses in exercise randomised controlled trials. Sports Medicine2017;46(5):699-713."), [55](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0055 "JosefssonT , LindwallM , ArcherT . Physical exercise intervention in depressive disorders: meta-analysis and systematic review. Scandinavian Journal of Medicine & Science in Sports2014;24(2):259-72."), [56](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0056 "BanyardH , EdwardKL , GarveyL , StephensonJ , AzevedoL , BensonAC . The effects of aerobic and resistance exercise on depression and anxiety: systematic review with meta-analysis. International Journal of Mental Health Nursing2025;34(3):e70054. [DOI: 10.1111/inm.70054]"), [57](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0057 "BuddeH , DolzN , Mueller-AlcazarA , SchachtF , VelasquesB , RibeiroP , et al. A 10 years update of effects of exercise on depression disorders-in otherwise healthy adults: a systematic review of meta-analyses and neurobiological mechanisms. PloS One2025;20(5):e0317610. [DOI: 10.1371/journal.pone.0317610]")\].

The increasing consideration given to exercise as an approach to managing depression has been reflected in recent clinical guidelines that have emerged from national and professional policy bodies, although the definition of exercise and the extent of recommendations differ. In England in 2022, the National Institute for Health and Care Excellence (NICE) published a guideline on the treatment and management of depression in adults \[[15](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0015 "NICE. Depression in adults: treatment and management. https://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/ng2222022.")\]. It advises that people doing any form of physical activity on a regular basis (e.g. walking, jogging, swimming, dance, gardening) could enhance their sense of wellbeing. Moreover, undertaking the activity outdoors can provide greater benefits. As a treatment option for both severe and mild‐to‐moderate depression, group physical activity interventions (usually for a group of eight participants) that are specifically designed for people with depression are recommended. These interventions should be provided by trained practitioners, usually consist of one session per week for 10 weeks, include moderate‐intensity aerobic exercise and not directly target thoughts and feelings \[[15](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0015 "NICE. Depression in adults: treatment and management. https://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/ng2222022.")\]. For people with more severe depression, consideration should be given to other treatment options and more contact with therapists should be considered carefully before recommending group exercise \[[15](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0015 "NICE. Depression in adults: treatment and management. https://www.nice.org.uk/guidance/ng2222022.")\]. The Royal Australian and New Zealand College of Psychiatrists (RANZCP) advises that exercise should be recommended to all patients due to the known health benefits \[[44](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0044 "MalhiGS , BellE , BassettD , BoyceP , BryantR , HazellP , et al. The 2020 Royal Australian and NewZealand College of Psychiatrists clinical practice guidelines for mood disorders. Australian and New Zealand Journal of Psychiatry2021;55(1):7-117. [DOI: 10.1177/0004867420979353]")\]. Although RANZCP recommend aerobic exercise, they recognise that a combination of aerobic and resistance exercise is probably optimal. RANZCP note some uncertainty around the optimal amount and intensity, indicating that it should be set at a level that demands sustained concentration and effort \[[58](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0058 "MalhiGS , BellE , BassettD , BoyceP , BryantR , HazellP , et al. The 2020 Royal Australian and New Zealand College of Psychiatrists clinical practice guidelines for mood disorders. Australian and New Zealand Journal of Psychiatry2021;55(1):7-117.")\]. The Canadian Network for Mood and Anxiety Treatments (CANMAT) recommends that supervised exercise of low to moderate intensity for 30 to 40 minutes per session, three to four times a week for at least nine weeks is effective as first‐line monotherapy for mild depression and as second‐line adjunctive treatment for moderate severity illness \[[29](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0029 "ParikhSV , SegalZV , GrigoriadisS , RavindranAV , KennedySH , LamRW , et al. Canadian Network for Mood and Anxiety Treatments (CANMAT) clinical guidelines for the management of major depressive disorder in adults. II. Psychotherapy alone or in combination with antidepressant medication. Journal of Affective Disorders2009;117(1):S15-S25."), [59](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0059 "RavindranAV , BalneavesLG , FaulknerG , OrtizA , McIntoshD , MorehouseRL , et al. Canadian network for mood and anxiety treatments (CANMAT) 2016 clinical guidelines for the management of adults with major depressive disorder: section 5. Complementary and alternative medicine treatments. Canadian Journal of Psychiatry2016;61(9):576-87."), [60](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0060 "LamRW , KennedySH , AdamsC , BahjiA , BeaulieuS , BhatV , et al. Canadian network for mood and anxiety treatments (CANMAT) 2023 update on clinical guidelines for management of major depressive disorder in adults [Réseau canadien pour les traitements de l'humeur et de l'anxiété (CANMAT) 2023: mise à jour des lignes directrices cliniques pour la prise en charge du trouble dépressif majeur chez les adultes]. Canadian Journal of Psychiatry. Revue Canadienne de Psychiatrie2024;69(9):641-87.")\]. Portuguese and Brazilian clinical guidance emphasises the benefits of exercise delivered by trained professionals as an option for treating depression, though it notes difficulties in implementation \[[61](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0061 "CarneiroLF , MotaMP , SchuchF , DeslandesA , Vasconcelos-RaposoJ . Portuguese and Brazilian guidelines for the treatment of depression: exercise as medicine. Brazilian Journal of Psychiatry2017;40(2):210-1.")\]. In contrast, guidance in the USA is equivocal. Although the American Psychiatric Association makes no specific recommendation concerning the role of exercise for treating depression, other agencies identify benefits associated with exercise in treating depression \[[24](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0024 "American Psychological Association. APA clinical practice guideline for the treatment of depression across three age cohorts. Available at https://www.apa.org/depression-guideline/guideline.pdf2019.")\]. The American Psychological Association recommends exercise as a monotherapy for adults with depression for whom psychotherapy or pharmacotherapy is ineffective or unacceptable \[[24](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0024 "American Psychological Association. APA clinical practice guideline for the treatment of depression across three age cohorts. Available at https://www.apa.org/depression-guideline/guideline.pdf2019.")\].

The focus of this systematic review is on assessing the effectiveness of exercise for treating depression. The review does not consider the influence of any referral schemes or broader programmes of care. The review will use the American College of Sports Medicine (ACSM) criteria to define the concept of exercise. Given that there are many forms of bodily movement or physical activity that differ in their characteristics, it is important to provide some clarity regarding those that will be included in this review.

Depression and low levels of physical activity have been shown to be closely associated in a two‐way relationship \[[62](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0062 "Roshanaei-MoghaddamB , KatonWJ , RussoJ . The longitudinal effects of depression on physical activity. General Hospital Psychiatry2009;31(4):306-15."), [63](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0063 "DubashS . The interplay of depression symptoms and physical activity: bidirectional insights from 25-years of the Americans' changing lives panel. Mental Health and Physical Activity2024;26:100599. [DOI: 10.1016/j.mhpa.2024.100599]")\]. While depression can lead to decreased levels of exercise through low motivation and energy, it is also evident that low levels of physical activity are a risk factor for people developing low mood and depression \[[62](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0062 "Roshanaei-MoghaddamB , KatonWJ , RussoJ . The longitudinal effects of depression on physical activity. General Hospital Psychiatry2009;31(4):306-15."), [64](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0064 "SmithPJ , BlumenthalJA . Exercise and physical activity in the prevention and treatment of depression. In: Handbook of Physical Activity and Mental Health. London: Routledge, 2013:145-60."), [65](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0065 "TeychenneM , BallK , SalmonJ . Physical activity and likelihood of depression in adults: a review. Preventive Medicine2008;46(5):397-411.")\]. Although such an association does not necessarily imply causality, there are plausible reasons why physical activity and exercise may improve mood \[[32](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0032 "CooneyGM , DwanK , GreigCA , LawlorDA , RimerJ , WaughFR , et al. Exercise for depression. Cochrane Database of Systematic Reviews2013, Issue 9. Art. No: CD004366. [DOI: 10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub6]"), [66](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0066 "WanjauMN , MöllerH , HaighF , MilatA , HayekR , LucasP , et al. Physical activity and depression and anxiety disorders: a systematic review of reviews and assessment of causality. AJPM Focus2023;2(2):100074. [DOI: 10.1016/j.focus.2023.100074]")\]. Exercise may act as a diversion from negative thoughts, and the mastery of a new skill may be important \[[67](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0067 "LePoreSJ . Expressive writing moderates the relation between intrusive thoughts and depressive symptoms. Journal of Personality and Social Psychology1997;73(5):1030-7.")\]. Social contact may be part of the mechanism of action \[[32](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0032 "CooneyGM , DwanK , GreigCA , LawlorDA , RimerJ , WaughFR , et al. Exercise for depression. Cochrane Database of Systematic Reviews2013, Issue 9. Art. No: CD004366. [DOI: 10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub6]")\]. Self‐efficacy may provide the mechanism by which exercise might have an antidepressant effect; people who experience an improvement in mood following exercise show higher self‐efficacy levels at three weeks and nine weeks post‐exercise \[[68](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0068 "CraftLL . Exercise and clinical depression: examining two psychological mechanisms. Psychology of Sport and Exercise2005;6:151-71.")\]. Self‐efficacy has been found to be intricately linked with self‐esteem, which, in turn, is considered to be one of the strongest predictors of overall subjective well‐being \[[69](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0069 "DienerE . Subjective well-being. Psychological Bulletin1984;95:542-75.")\]. Low self‐esteem is also considered to be closely related to mental illness \[[70](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0070 "FoxKR . The effects of exercise on self-perceptions and self-esteem. In: BiddleSJ , FoxKR , editor(s). Physical Activity and Psychological Well-Being. London: Routledge, 2000:88-117.")\]. It has been shown that exercise has a direct positive effect on levels of self‐esteem, which occurred prior to improvements in depressive symptoms \[[71](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0071 "ParkSH , HanKS , KangCB . Effects of exercise programs on depressive symptoms, quality of life, and self-esteem in older people: a systematic review of randomized controlled trials. Applied Nursing Research2014;27(4):219-26."), [72](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0072 "YìğìterK . The effects of participation in regular exercise on self-esteem and hopelessness of female university students. Social Behavior and Personality: an International Journal2014;42(2):1233-43."), [73](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0073 "LegrandFD . Effects of exercise on physical self-concept, global self-esteem, and depression in women of low socioeconomic status with elevated depressive symptoms. Journal of Sport & Exercise Psychology2014;36(4):357-65.")\]. Physical activity may have physiological effects, such as changes in endorphin and monoamine levels \[[74](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0074 "Gomez-MerinoD , BéquetF , BerthelotM , ChennaouiM , GuezennecCY . Site-dependent effects of an acute intensive exercise on extracellular 5-HT and 5-HIAA levels in rat brain. Neuroscience Letters2001;301(2):143–6.")\], or reduction in the levels of the stress hormone cortisol \[[75](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0075 "ChenMJ . The neurobiology of depression and physical exercise. In: Handbook of Physical Activity and Mental Health. London: Routledge, 2013:169-84.")\], all of which may improve mood. Exercise stimulates the growth of new nerve cells and the release of proteins known to improve the health and survival of nerve cells, for example, brain‐derived growth neurotrophic factor \[[76](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0076 "CotmanCW , BerchtoldNC . Exercise: a behavioural intervention to enhance brain health and plasticity. Trends in Neurosciences2002;25(6):295-301."), [77](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0077 "ErnstC , OlsonAK , PinelJP , LamRW , ChristieBR . Antidepressant effects of exercise: evidence for an adult neurogenesis hypothesis?Journal of Psychiatry and Neurosciences2006;31(2):84-92."), [78](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0078 "LuJ , XuY , HuW , GaoY , NiX , ShengH , et al. Exercise ameliorates depression-like behavior and increases hippocampal BDNF level in ovariectomized rats. Neuroscience Letters2014;573:13-18."), [79](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0079 "YauSY , LauBW , TongJB , WongR , ChingYP , QiuG , et al. Hippocampal neurogenesis and dendritic plasticity support running-improved spatial learning and depression-like behaviour in stressed rats. PloS One2011;6(9):e24263. [DOI: 10.1371/journal.pone.0024263]")\]. Low brain‐derived neurotrophic factor levels can be seen in untreated patients suffering major depression compared to healthy controls \[[80](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0080 "Ristevska-DimitrovskaG , ShishkovR , GerazovaVP , VujovikV , StefanovskiB , NovotniA , et al. Different serum BDNF levels in depression: results from BDNF studies in FYR Macedonia and Bulgaria. Psychiatria Danubina2013;25(2):123-7."), [81](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0081 "SenS , DumanR , SanacoraG . Serum brain-derived neurotrophic factor, depression, and antidepressant medications: meta-analyses and implications. Biological Psychiatry2008;64(4):527-32.")\]. This positive effect of exercise on low brain‐derived neurotrophic factor levels has been seen specifically in patients suffering from depression \[[82](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0082 "HeymanE , GamelinFX , GoekintM , PiscitelliF , RoelandsB , LeclairE , et al. Intense exercise increases circulating endocannabinoid and BDNF levels in humans--possible implications for reward and depression. Psychoneuroendocrinology2012;37(6):844-51."), [83](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0083 "LaskeC , BanschbachS , StranskyE , BoschS , StratenG , MachannJ , et al. Exercise-induced normalization of decreased BDNF serum concentration in elderly women with remitted major depression. International Journal of Neuropsychopharmacology2010;13(5):595-602.")\].

### Why it is important to do this review

Despite several new systematic reviews and meta‐analyses on this topic ([53](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0053 "DanielssonL , NorasAM , WaernM , CarlssonJ . Exercise in the treatment of major depression: a systematic review grading the quality of evidence. Physiotherapy Theory and Practice2013;29(8):573-85."), [52](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0052 "FarahWH , AlsawasM , MainouM , AlahdabF , FarahMH , AhmedAT , et al. Non-pharmacological treatment of depression: a systematic review and evidence map. Evidence-based Medicine2016;21(6):214-21."), [84](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0084 "KvamS , KleppeCL , NordhusIH , HovlandA . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis. Journal of Affective Disorders2016;202:67-86."), [51](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0051 "SchuchFB , VancampfortD , RichardsJ , RosenbaumS , WardPB , StubbsB . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis adjusting for publication bias. Journal of Psychiatric Research2016;77:42-51."), [85](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0085 "SchuchFB , DunnAL , KanitzAC , DelevattiRS , FleckMP . Moderators of response in exercise treatment for depression: a systematic review. Journal of Affective Disorders2016;195:40-9."), [49](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0049 "SilveiraH , MoraesH , OliveiraN , CoutinhoES , LaksJ , DeslandesA . Physical exercise and clinically depressed patients: a systematic review and meta-analysis. Neuropsychobiology2013;67(2):61-8."), [50](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0050 "De Souza MouraAM , LamegoMK , PaesF , Ferreira RochaNB , Simoes-SilvaV , RochaSA , et al. Comparison among aerobic exercise and other types of interventions to treat depression: a systematic review. CNS & Neurological Disorders - Drug Targets2015;14(9):1171-83."), [54](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0054 "StubbsB , VancampfortD , RosenbaumS , WardPB , RichardsJ , UssherM , et al. Challenges establishing the efficacy of exercise as an antidepressant treatment: a systematic review and meta-analysis of control group responses in exercise randomised controlled trials. Sports Medicine2017;46(5):699-713."), [55](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0055 "JosefssonT , LindwallM , ArcherT . Physical exercise intervention in depressive disorders: meta-analysis and systematic review. Scandinavian Journal of Medicine & Science in Sports2014;24(2):259-72."), [86](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0086 "BaileyAP , HetrickSE , RosenbaumS , PurcellR , ParkerAG . Treating depression with physical activity in adolescents and young adults: a systematic review and meta-analysis of randomised controlled trials. Psychological Medicine2018;48(7):1068-83. [DOI: 10.1017/S0033291717002653]"), [87](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0087 "Correia ÉM, MonteiroD , BentoT , RodriguesF , CidL , VitorinoA , et al. Analysis of the effect of different physical exercise protocols on depression in adults: systematic review and meta-analysis of randomized controlled trials. Sports Health2024;16(2):285-94."), [88](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0088 "GuoS , LiuF , ShenJ , WeiM , YangY . Comparative efficacy of seven exercise interventions for symptoms of depression in college students: a network of meta-analysis. Medicine2020;99(47):e23058. [DOI: 10.1097/MD.0000000000023058]"), [89](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0089 "HeisselA , HeinenD , BrokmeierLL , SkarabisN , KangasM , VancampfortD , et al. Exercise as medicine for depressive symptoms? A systematic review and meta-analysis with meta-regression. British Journal of Sports Medicine2023;57(16):1049-57."), [90](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0090 "JazayeriD , ZanjaniZ , JoekarS , AlvaniSR , MolaeiA . Comparison study of the effects of resistance and endurance exercise interventions for the treatment of depression: a meta-analytical review. Journal of Contemporary Psychotherapy2022;52:237-46. [DOI: 10.1007/s10879-022-09537-8]"), [91](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0091 "KroghJ , HjorthøjC , SpeyerH , GluudC , NordentoftM . Exercise for patients with major depression: a systematic review with meta-analysis and trial sequential analysis. BMJ Open2017;7(9):e014820. [DOI: 10.1136/bmjopen-2016-014820]"), [92](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0092 "LeeJ , GiercM , Vila-RodriguezF , PutermanE , FaulknerG . Efficacy of exercise combined with standard treatment for depression compared to standard treatment alone: a systematic review and meta-analysis of randomized controlled trials. Journal of Affective Disorders2021;295:1494–511."), [93](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0093 "MorresID , HatzigeorgiadisA , StathiA , ComoutosN , Arpin-CribbieC , KrommidasC , et al. Aerobic exercise for adult patients with major depressive disorder in mental health services: a systematic review and meta-analysis. Depression and Anxiety2019;36:39-53. [DOI: 10.1002/da.22842]"), [94](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0094 "NoetelM , SandersT , Gallardo-GómezD , TaylorP , Del Pozo CruzB , Van den HoekD , et al. Effect of exercise for depression: systematic review and network meta-analysis of randomised controlled trials. BMJ (Clinical Research Ed.)2024;384:e075847. [DOI: 10.1136/bmj-2023-075847]"), [95](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0095 "Pérez-LópezFR , Martínez-DomínguezaSJ , LajusticiaH , ChedrauicP . Effects of programmed exercise on depressive symptoms in midlife and older women: a meta-analysis of randomized controlled trials. Maturitas2017;106:38-47."), [96](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0096 "RecchiaF , LeungCK , ChinEC , FongDY , MonteroD , ChengCP , et al. Comparative effectiveness of exercise, antidepressants and their combination in treating non-severe depression: a systematic review and network meta-analysis of randomised controlled trials. British Journal of Sports Medicine2022;56(23):1375-80."), [97](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0097 "ZhangZ , LiuJY , ZhuKT , HuoGQ . A META analysis and systematic review of the effects of exercise interventions on middle-aged and elderly patients with depression. PloS One2025;20(1):e0303594. [DOI: 10.1371/journal.pone.0303594]")), doubts remain about whether exercise is beneficial in treating depression when compared to other treatment options (and if it is, the extent of that benefit and what type of exercise benefits what type of person \[[43](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0043 "EkkekakisP . Honey, I shrunk the pooled SMD! Guide to critical appraisal of systematic reviews and meta-analyses using the Cochrane review on exercise for depression as example. Mental Health and Physical Activity2015;8:21-36."), [51](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0051 "SchuchFB , VancampfortD , RichardsJ , RosenbaumS , WardPB , StubbsB . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis adjusting for publication bias. Journal of Psychiatric Research2016;77:42-51."), [84](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0084 "KvamS , KleppeCL , NordhusIH , HovlandA . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis. Journal of Affective Disorders2016;202:67-86.")\]). This uncertainty is reflected in differences in the pooled estimates of the comparative effects of exercise for treating depression, which range from statistically significant benefit (standardised mean difference (SMD) −1.13, 95% confidence interval (CI) −1.48 to −0.78) to no difference (SMD −0.14, 95% CI −0.16 to 0.12) \[[57](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0057 "BuddeH , DolzN , Mueller-AlcazarA , SchachtF , VelasquesB , RibeiroP , et al. A 10 years update of effects of exercise on depression disorders-in otherwise healthy adults: a systematic review of meta-analyses and neurobiological mechanisms. PloS One2025;20(5):e0317610. [DOI: 10.1371/journal.pone.0317610]")\].

Underlying the uncertainties and ongoing debate are differences in the scope of and methods used by systematic reviews and meta‐analyses: elements that vary include type (e.g. aerobic only \[[50](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0050 "De Souza MouraAM , LamegoMK , PaesF , Ferreira RochaNB , Simoes-SilvaV , RochaSA , et al. Comparison among aerobic exercise and other types of interventions to treat depression: a systematic review. CNS & Neurological Disorders - Drug Targets2015;14(9):1171-83."), [53](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0053 "DanielssonL , NorasAM , WaernM , CarlssonJ . Exercise in the treatment of major depression: a systematic review grading the quality of evidence. Physiotherapy Theory and Practice2013;29(8):573-85."), [93](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0093 "MorresID , HatzigeorgiadisA , StathiA , ComoutosN , Arpin-CribbieC , KrommidasC , et al. Aerobic exercise for adult patients with major depressive disorder in mental health services: a systematic review and meta-analysis. Depression and Anxiety2019;36:39-53. [DOI: 10.1002/da.22842]")\], aerobic or strength \[[49](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0049 "SilveiraH , MoraesH , OliveiraN , CoutinhoES , LaksJ , DeslandesA . Physical exercise and clinically depressed patients: a systematic review and meta-analysis. Neuropsychobiology2013;67(2):61-8.")\], inclusion of yoga, stretching, tai chi and qigong \[[50](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0050 "De Souza MouraAM , LamegoMK , PaesF , Ferreira RochaNB , Simoes-SilvaV , RochaSA , et al. Comparison among aerobic exercise and other types of interventions to treat depression: a systematic review. CNS & Neurological Disorders - Drug Targets2015;14(9):1171-83.")\] or all types of exercise \[[51](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0051 "SchuchFB , VancampfortD , RichardsJ , RosenbaumS , WardPB , StubbsB . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis adjusting for publication bias. Journal of Psychiatric Research2016;77:42-51."), [52](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0052 "FarahWH , AlsawasM , MainouM , AlahdabF , FarahMH , AhmedAT , et al. Non-pharmacological treatment of depression: a systematic review and evidence map. Evidence-based Medicine2016;21(6):214-21."), [54](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0054 "StubbsB , VancampfortD , RosenbaumS , WardPB , RichardsJ , UssherM , et al. Challenges establishing the efficacy of exercise as an antidepressant treatment: a systematic review and meta-analysis of control group responses in exercise randomised controlled trials. Sports Medicine2017;46(5):699-713."), [55](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0055 "JosefssonT , LindwallM , ArcherT . Physical exercise intervention in depressive disorders: meta-analysis and systematic review. Scandinavian Journal of Medicine & Science in Sports2014;24(2):259-72."), [84](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0084 "KvamS , KleppeCL , NordhusIH , HovlandA . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis. Journal of Affective Disorders2016;202:67-86."), [87](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0087 "Correia ÉM, MonteiroD , BentoT , RodriguesF , CidL , VitorinoA , et al. Analysis of the effect of different physical exercise protocols on depression in adults: systematic review and meta-analysis of randomized controlled trials. Sports Health2024;16(2):285-94.")\]), treatment strategy used (e.g. alone \[[84](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0084 "KvamS , KleppeCL , NordhusIH , HovlandA . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis. Journal of Affective Disorders2016;202:67-86.")\], as an adjunct/combination therapy \[[84](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0084 "KvamS , KleppeCL , NordhusIH , HovlandA . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis. Journal of Affective Disorders2016;202:67-86.")\] or both/undefined \[[49](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0049 "SilveiraH , MoraesH , OliveiraN , CoutinhoES , LaksJ , DeslandesA . Physical exercise and clinically depressed patients: a systematic review and meta-analysis. Neuropsychobiology2013;67(2):61-8."), [50](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0050 "De Souza MouraAM , LamegoMK , PaesF , Ferreira RochaNB , Simoes-SilvaV , RochaSA , et al. Comparison among aerobic exercise and other types of interventions to treat depression: a systematic review. CNS & Neurological Disorders - Drug Targets2015;14(9):1171-83."), [53](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0053 "DanielssonL , NorasAM , WaernM , CarlssonJ . Exercise in the treatment of major depression: a systematic review grading the quality of evidence. Physiotherapy Theory and Practice2013;29(8):573-85."), [54](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0054 "StubbsB , VancampfortD , RosenbaumS , WardPB , RichardsJ , UssherM , et al. Challenges establishing the efficacy of exercise as an antidepressant treatment: a systematic review and meta-analysis of control group responses in exercise randomised controlled trials. Sports Medicine2017;46(5):699-713.")\]) and definition (e.g. physical exercise \[[50](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0050 "De Souza MouraAM , LamegoMK , PaesF , Ferreira RochaNB , Simoes-SilvaV , RochaSA , et al. Comparison among aerobic exercise and other types of interventions to treat depression: a systematic review. CNS & Neurological Disorders - Drug Targets2015;14(9):1171-83."), [51](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0051 "SchuchFB , VancampfortD , RichardsJ , RosenbaumS , WardPB , StubbsB . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis adjusting for publication bias. Journal of Psychiatric Research2016;77:42-51.")\], physical activity \[[54](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0054 "StubbsB , VancampfortD , RosenbaumS , WardPB , RichardsJ , UssherM , et al. Challenges establishing the efficacy of exercise as an antidepressant treatment: a systematic review and meta-analysis of control group responses in exercise randomised controlled trials. Sports Medicine2017;46(5):699-713.")\]). In contrast, in this review, we have not defined the frequency, duration and intensity of treatment or limited inclusion by these factors.

Comparator interventions have also differed in different systematic reviews. They have included active pharmacological interventions (e.g. antidepressants) \[[50](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0050 "De Souza MouraAM , LamegoMK , PaesF , Ferreira RochaNB , Simoes-SilvaV , RochaSA , et al. Comparison among aerobic exercise and other types of interventions to treat depression: a systematic review. CNS & Neurological Disorders - Drug Targets2015;14(9):1171-83."), [53](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0053 "DanielssonL , NorasAM , WaernM , CarlssonJ . Exercise in the treatment of major depression: a systematic review grading the quality of evidence. Physiotherapy Theory and Practice2013;29(8):573-85."), [84](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0084 "KvamS , KleppeCL , NordhusIH , HovlandA . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis. Journal of Affective Disorders2016;202:67-86.")\] and non‐pharmacological interventions (e.g. psychotherapy, psychoeducation, physical activity/exercise) \[[50](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0050 "De Souza MouraAM , LamegoMK , PaesF , Ferreira RochaNB , Simoes-SilvaV , RochaSA , et al. Comparison among aerobic exercise and other types of interventions to treat depression: a systematic review. CNS & Neurological Disorders - Drug Targets2015;14(9):1171-83."), [52](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0052 "FarahWH , AlsawasM , MainouM , AlahdabF , FarahMH , AhmedAT , et al. Non-pharmacological treatment of depression: a systematic review and evidence map. Evidence-based Medicine2016;21(6):214-21."), [53](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0053 "DanielssonL , NorasAM , WaernM , CarlssonJ . Exercise in the treatment of major depression: a systematic review grading the quality of evidence. Physiotherapy Theory and Practice2013;29(8):573-85."), [84](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0084 "KvamS , KleppeCL , NordhusIH , HovlandA . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis. Journal of Affective Disorders2016;202:67-86.")\], non‐active interventions (e.g. placebo) \[[51](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0051 "SchuchFB , VancampfortD , RichardsJ , RosenbaumS , WardPB , StubbsB . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis adjusting for publication bias. Journal of Psychiatric Research2016;77:42-51."), [55](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0055 "JosefssonT , LindwallM , ArcherT . Scandinavian Journal of Medicine & Science in Sports2014;24(2):259-72."), [84](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0084 "KvamS , KleppeCL , NordhusIH , HovlandA . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis. Journal of Affective Disorders2016;202:67-86.")\], alternative therapies (e.g. meditation, relaxation, bright light therapy \[[50](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0050 "De Souza MouraAM , LamegoMK , PaesF , Ferreira RochaNB , Simoes-SilvaV , RochaSA , et al. Comparison among aerobic exercise and other types of interventions to treat depression: a systematic review. CNS & Neurological Disorders - Drug Targets2015;14(9):1171-83."), [98](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0098 "StathopoulouG , PowersMB , BerryAC , SmitsJA , OttoMW . Exercise interventions for mental health: a quantitative and qualitative review. Clinical Psychology: Science and Practice2006;13:179-93."), [99](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0099 "MeadGE , MorleyW , CampbellP , GreigCA , McMurdoM , LawlorDA . Exercise for depression. Cochrane Database of Systematic Reviews2009, Issue 3. Art. No: CD004366. [DOI: 10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub4]"), [100](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0100 "RethorstCD , WipfliBM , LandersDM . The antidepressive effects of exercise. Sports Medicine (Auckland, N.Z.)2009;39(6):491-511."), [101](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0101 "KroghJ , NordentoftM , SterneJ , LawlorDA . The effect of exercise in clinical depressed adults: systematic review and meta-analysis of randomised controlled trials. Journal of Clinical Psychiatry2011;72(4):529-38.")\]), usual care \[[51](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0051 "SchuchFB , VancampfortD , RichardsJ , RosenbaumS , WardPB , StubbsB . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis adjusting for publication bias. Journal of Psychiatric Research2016;77:42-51."), [52](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0052 "FarahWH , AlsawasM , MainouM , AlahdabF , FarahMH , AhmedAT , et al. Evidence-based Medicine2016;21(6):214-21."), [53](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0053 "DanielssonL , NorasAM , WaernM , CarlssonJ . Physiotherapy Theory and Practice2013;29(8):573-85."), [55](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0055 "JosefssonT , LindwallM , ArcherT . Physical exercise intervention in depressive disorders: meta-analysis and systematic review. Scandinavian Journal of Medicine & Science in Sports2014;24(2):259-72."), [84](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0084 "KvamS , KleppeCL , NordhusIH , HovlandA . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis. Journal of Affective Disorders2016;202:67-86.")\], no treatment/waiting list controls \[[51](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0051 "SchuchFB , VancampfortD , RichardsJ , RosenbaumS , WardPB , StubbsB . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis adjusting for publication bias. Journal of Psychiatric Research2016;77:42-51."), [55](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0055 "JosefssonT , LindwallM , ArcherT . Physical exercise intervention in depressive disorders: meta-analysis and systematic review. Scandinavian Journal of Medicine & Science in Sports2014;24(2):259-72.")\], or no comparator has been stated \[[49](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0049 "SilveiraH , MoraesH , OliveiraN , CoutinhoES , LaksJ , DeslandesA . Physical exercise and clinically depressed patients: a systematic review and meta-analysis. Neuropsychobiology2013;67(2):61-8.")\].

Despite these systematic reviews all having a focus on adults with major depressive disorders, the criteria used for diagnosing depression, and for establishing its severity, have varied. Importantly, these criteria were often the primary outcome measures for assessing the effectiveness of the interventions. Diagnosis has occurred through clinical interviews \[[53](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0053 "DanielssonL , NorasAM , WaernM , CarlssonJ . Exercise in the treatment of major depression: a systematic review grading the quality of evidence. Physiotherapy Theory and Practice2013;29(8):573-85.")\], occurrence of unspecified depression or depressive symptoms \[[55](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0055 "JosefssonT , LindwallM , ArcherT . Physical exercise intervention in depressive disorders: meta-analysis and systematic review. Scandinavian Journal of Medicine & Science in Sports2014;24(2):259-72.")\] or the use of different combinations of clinical interviews, diagnostic systems (DSM‐IV, ICD‐10, Research Diagnostic Criteria), self‐reported depression scales using different thresholds (validated or unvalidated) (e.g. Beck Depression Inventory, Hamilton Rating Scale for Depression, exercise self‐efficacy, depression coping self‐efficacy) \[[49](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0049 "SilveiraH , MoraesH , OliveiraN , CoutinhoES , LaksJ , DeslandesA . Physical exercise and clinically depressed patients: a systematic review and meta-analysis. Neuropsychobiology2013;67(2):61-8."), [50](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0050 "De Souza MouraAM , LamegoMK , PaesF , Ferreira RochaNB , Simoes-SilvaV , RochaSA , et al. Comparison among aerobic exercise and other types of interventions to treat depression: a systematic review. CNS & Neurological Disorders - Drug Targets2015;14(9):1171-83."), [51](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0051 "SchuchFB , VancampfortD , RichardsJ , RosenbaumS , WardPB , StubbsB . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis adjusting for publication bias. Journal of Psychiatric Research2016;77:42-51."), [54](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0054 "StubbsB , VancampfortD , RosenbaumS , WardPB , RichardsJ , UssherM , et al. Challenges establishing the efficacy of exercise as an antidepressant treatment: a systematic review and meta-analysis of control group responses in exercise randomised controlled trials. Sports Medicine2017;46(5):699-713."), [55](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0055 "JosefssonT , LindwallM , ArcherT . Physical exercise intervention in depressive disorders: meta-analysis and systematic review. Scandinavian Journal of Medicine & Science in Sports2014;24(2):259-72.")\], with some variation in interpretation by researchers and/or clinicians. Depressive conditions also varied in the different reviews, whether by specifying levels of severity required for inclusion \[[49](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0049 "SilveiraH , MoraesH , OliveiraN , CoutinhoES , LaksJ , DeslandesA . Physical exercise and clinically depressed patients: a systematic review and meta-analysis. Neuropsychobiology2013;67(2):61-8.")\], excluding multiple diagnoses \[[55](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0055 "JosefssonT , LindwallM , ArcherT . Physical exercise intervention in depressive disorders: meta-analysis and systematic review. Scandinavian Journal of Medicine & Science in Sports2014;24(2):259-72.")\], focusing on unipolar depression only \[[52](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0052 "FarahWH , AlsawasM , MainouM , AlahdabF , FarahMH , AhmedAT , et al. Non-pharmacological treatment of depression: a systematic review and evidence map. Evidence-based Medicine2016;21(6):214-21.")\], or including unipolar, bipolar and dysthymia \[[51](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0051 "SchuchFB , VancampfortD , RichardsJ , RosenbaumS , WardPB , StubbsB . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis adjusting for publication bias. Journal of Psychiatric Research2016;77:42-51."), [54](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0054 "StubbsB , VancampfortD , RosenbaumS , WardPB , RichardsJ , UssherM , et al. Challenges establishing the efficacy of exercise as an antidepressant treatment: a systematic review and meta-analysis of control group responses in exercise randomised controlled trials. Sports Medicine2017;46(5):699-713.")\]. In some instances, participants were included who had depression diagnosed as a comorbidity, with another condition as the main diagnosis \[[100](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0100 "RethorstCD , WipfliBM , LandersDM . The antidepressive effects of exercise. Sports Medicine (Auckland, N.Z.)2009;39(6):491-511.")\].

Evidence synthesised in the previous systematic reviews on this topic originated from studies that differ in their design and methodological rigour, raising concerns about risk of bias \[[55](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0055 "JosefssonT , LindwallM , ArcherT . Physical exercise intervention in depressive disorders: meta-analysis and systematic review. Scandinavian Journal of Medicine & Science in Sports2014;24(2):259-72.")\]. Many focused solely on randomised controlled trials (RCTs) \[[50](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0050 "De Souza MouraAM , LamegoMK , PaesF , Ferreira RochaNB , Simoes-SilvaV , RochaSA , et al. Comparison among aerobic exercise and other types of interventions to treat depression: a systematic review. CNS & Neurological Disorders - Drug Targets2015;14(9):1171-83."), [51](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0051 "SchuchFB , VancampfortD , RichardsJ , RosenbaumS , WardPB , StubbsB . Exercise as a treatment for depression: a meta-analysis adjusting for publication bias. Journal of Psychiatric Research2016;77:42-51."), [52](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0052 "FarahWH , AlsawasM , MainouM , AlahdabF , FarahMH , AhmedAT , et al. Non-pharmacological treatment of depression: a systematic review and evidence map. Evidence-based Medicine2016;21(6):214-21."), [53](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0053 "DanielssonL , NorasAM , WaernM , CarlssonJ . Exercise in the treatment of major depression: a systematic review grading the quality of evidence. Physiotherapy Theory and Practice2013;29(8):573-85."), [54](https://www.cochranelibrary.com/cdsr/doi/10.1002/14651858.CD004366.pub7/#CD004366-bib-0054 "StubbsB , VancampfortD , RosenbaumS , WardPB , RichardsJ , UssherM , et al.
